# GB 12052-89 to Unicode table (complete)
# Made by Jaemin Chung
# Unicode Version 7.0
# Date: 2014-12-20

# This file is encoded in UTF-8.

# 1. Most of the characters at 53-01 through 71-86 map to sequences of two or three Unicode code points.
#
# 2. Twenty-three (23) characters share the same Unicode mappings with other characters.
#
# 2-1. The following pair maps to the same Unicode code point.
# 01-71	0x2167	0xA1E7	U+FF04	# ＄
# 03-04	0x2324	0xA3A4	U+FF04	# ＄
# When converting Unicode back to GB 12052-89, it is recommended to use the first one (01-71).
#
# 2-2. The characters at 71-41 through 71-64 use a different typeface style (Hunminjeongeum Haerye style).
# For example, 35-80 and 71-41 both correspond to U+314F ㅏ, but the former uses a normal typeface style and the latter uses a different typeface style.
# As they only differ in their typeface style, no attempt was made to make their mappings unique (thus, 22 characters share the mappings with other characters).
# Instead, the ones with a different typeface style are given a comment "Hunminjeongeum Haerye style".
# Here are some examples from the data:
# 35-80	0x4370	0xC3F0	U+314F	# ㅏ
# 71-41	0x6749	0xE7C9	U+314F	# ㅏ; Hunminjeongeum Haerye style
# 36-02	0x4422	0xC4A2	U+3151	# ㅑ
# 71-42	0x674A	0xE7CA	U+3151	# ㅑ; Hunminjeongeum Haerye style
# 36-14	0x442E	0xC4AE	U+3153	# ㅓ
# 71-43	0x674B	0xE7CB	U+3153	# ㅓ; Hunminjeongeum Haerye style
# When converting Unicode back to GB 12052-89, it is recommended to use the ones with normal typeface style (that is, ones without "Hunminjeongeum Haerye style"; 35-80, 36-02, 36-14, etc.).
# However, 71-58 can be mapped directly to U+3187 ㆇ, because there is no corresponding character with the normal typeface style.
#
# 3. The following 20 characters use the hangul jamo that were added in Unicode 5.2 (October 2009).
# In environments that do not properly support Unicode 5.2 and above, these characters may not be rendered correctly.
